## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws describing elastic/plastic deformation and thermal softening/thermal strain effects in solids.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elastic response with E(T) approx. linear in T)
- Exponential thermal softening of elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness decreases with temperature)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain offset: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal expansion strain)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial (Landau-type expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate nonlinearity in stress–strain)
- Temperature-coupled nonlinear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon + c3 * epsilon**2 (E depends on T and nonlinearity in epsilon)
- Hollomon/Ludwik strain hardening with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (plastic hardening with thermal softening of strength coefficient)
- Ramberg–Osgood-like direct stress form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (empirical elastic + power-law hardening without explicitly solving for sigma)
- Voce-type saturating hardening with thermal scaling: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) - c2 * exp(-c3 * epsilon) (hardening approaches a saturation stress that softens with T)
- Elastic–perfectly plastic (yield stress depends on T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon for epsilon <= c2 + c3 * T; sigma = c4 * exp(-c5 * T) for epsilon > c2 + c3 * T (piecewise yield with thermal softening)
- Reduced Johnson–Cook-style thermal softening factor (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T + c4)**c5) (multiplicative separation: strain hardening times normalized thermal softening)
- Large-strain hyperelastic (1D neo-Hookean-like, with T-dependent shear modulus): sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * ((1 + epsilon) - (1 + epsilon)**(-2)) (captures stretch-based nonlinearity via reciprocal powers)
- Glass-transition-like sigmoidal modulus drop: sigma = (c0 * epsilon) / (1 + exp(c1 * (T - c2))) (stiffness transitions sharply over a temperature interval)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elasticity typically implies sigma is approximately proportional to epsilon, with the proportionality (Young’s modulus) potentially varying with T.
- Thermal softening is often modeled by making stiffness or yield/flow stress decrease with T (commonly linear-in-T over a narrow range, or exponential-in-T over wider ranges).
- Thermal expansion under constraint introduces an effective shift in strain, so sigma depends on (epsilon - alpha*(T - T0)), yielding near-zero stress when mechanical strain matches free thermal strain.
- Plastic strain hardening commonly produces convex-increasing sigma(epsilon), frequently captured by power laws in (epsilon + offset).
- Many metals show saturation of hardening at large strains; an exponential-in-epsilon approach to a limiting stress is a common structural signature.
- Yielding can create a change in slope of sigma vs epsilon (elastic slope to post-yield slope), motivating piecewise or smoothly blended formulations.
- At large deformations, stress often depends on stretch ratios (1 + epsilon) and their reciprocals, motivating terms like (1+epsilon) and (1+epsilon)^(-k).
- Near phase transitions (e.g., glass transition in polymers), stiffness can change rapidly over a narrow T interval, often represented by sigmoidal temperature dependence.
- A common separability assumption in thermomechanical constitutive laws is sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), reflecting temperature scaling of a base stress–strain curve.

Variable roles: T appears only multiplicatively with ε (in T*c0*ε) and inside exponentials exp(c3 T), exp(c9 T), while ε appears linearly and in the rational numerator/denominator; the denominator (0.1688ε+0.2072) stays positive for typical ε so the rational terms act like smooth saturation/curvature in ε. With fitted values, the dominant ε dependence is from large coefficients c1≈1897.5 and c8≈-1276.1 (partly modulated by exp(-0.0017515T)), while the T-only exponential term has moderate magnitude (c2≈-41.3) and both exponent rates are small (|c3|,|c9|≈2e-3), so for moderate T the model is approximately equivalent to a rational-in-ε correction plus an almost-linear-in-T adjustment: ≈ (c1ε + c0 Tε) + c2(1+c3T) + c4ε/(c5ε+c6) + c7/(c5ε+c6) + c8ε(1+c9T).

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon*(-c3*(T - c4) + c5) + c6*(T - c7)*log(epsilon + c8)
Candidate formulas: 67

GT (with fixed constants) is
\[
F(\epsilon,T)=11.1190537583\,\epsilon^2+11.1190537583\,\epsilon\big(-0.09195630170\,(T-352.0084637)+1\big)+4.3699183275\,(T-352.0084637)\,\log(\epsilon+1).
\]
Rewrite to expose basis functions:
- Polynomial part:
\[
11.1190537583\,\epsilon^2 + 11.1190537583\,\epsilon\,(1-0.09195630170\,T+0.09195630170\cdot 352.0084637)
\]
So it contains **\(\epsilon^2\)** and **\(T\epsilon\)** and **\(\epsilon\)** terms.
- Log part:
\[
4.3699183275\,T\log(\epsilon+1) - 4.3699183275\cdot 352.0084637\,\log(\epsilon+1)
\]
So it contains **\(T\log(\epsilon+1)\)** and **\(\log(\epsilon+1)\)**.

Therefore any exactly-matching candidate must be able (after choosing its free constants) to represent simultaneously the independent basis functions:
\[
\epsilon^2,\quad T\epsilon,\quad \epsilon,\quad T\log(\epsilon+1),\quad \log(\epsilon+1),
\]
with the **log argument exactly \(\epsilon+1\)** (up to the allowed Abs simplification, but Abs only affects \(\epsilon\), not \(\epsilon+1\)) and with **no extra non-polynomial/non-log dependence** (like \(\exp(T\cdot)\), \(\sin\), rational-in-\(\epsilon\) terms) unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

Now check candidates:

1) Has \(T\epsilon\), \(\epsilon\), rationals in \(\epsilon\), and exponentials in \(T\). No \(\epsilon^2\) and no \(\log(\epsilon+1)\). Cannot match.  
2) Linear in \(\epsilon\) plus exponentials in \(T\) and \(\exp(c4\epsilon)\). No \(\epsilon^2\), no log. Cannot.

**GT:** `11.119*epsilon^2 + 11.119*epsilon*(-0.0920*(T - 352.0) + 1) + 4.370*(T - 352.0)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Let me expand the GT:
- `11.119*epsilon^2 + 11.119*epsilon - 11.119*0.0920*epsilon*(T - 352.0) + 4.370*(T - 352.0)*log(epsilon + 1)`
- `= 11.119*epsilon^2 + 11.119*epsilon - 1.0227*epsilon*T + 1.0227*352.0*epsilon + 4.370*T*log(epsilon+1) - 4.370*352.0*log(epsilon+1)`
- `= 11.119*epsilon^2 - 1.0227*T*epsilon + (11.119 + 359.99)*epsilon + 4.370*T*log(epsilon+1) - 1538.2*log(epsilon+1)`
- `= 11.119*epsilon^2 - 1.0227*T*epsilon + 371.11*epsilon + 4.370*T*log(epsilon+1) - 1538.2*log(epsilon+1)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `epsilon^2`
2. `T*epsilon`
3. `epsilon`
4. `T*log(epsilon+1)`
5. `log(epsilon+1)`

This is a specific combination of polynomial terms in epsilon and T, plus logarithmic terms.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of these exact basis functions.

For a candidate to match, it must be expressible with exactly these basis functions (or equivalent). Key features:
- **`epsilon^2` term** (or equivalent)
- **`T*epsilon` term**
- **`epsilon` term**
- **`T*log(epsilon+1)` term**
- **`log(epsilon+1)` term**

No exponential functions in T should appear (unless they can be zeroed out), no sin/cos terms, etc.

Let me systematically check candidates that have `log(epsilon+1)` or similar terms, and `epsilon^2` or equivalent:

**Candidate 34:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*exp(T*c3) + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon + c8) + c9/(c7*epsilon + c8)`

**Candidate 8:** `T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c1*exp(T*c2) + c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*exp(T*c6) + c7`

Has `log(c4*epsilon+1)` but no `T*log(epsilon+1)`. Has `exp(T*c2)` and `exp(T*c6)`. Missing `T*epsilon` and `epsilon^2`. No match.

**Candidate 3:** `T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c1*exp(T*c2) + c3*exp(T*c4) + c5 + c6*exp(T*c7)*log(c8*|epsilon| + 1)`

The term `c6*exp(T*c7)*log(c8*|epsilon|+1)` - if we set c7=0, this becomes `c6*log(c8*epsilon+1)`, giving no T dependence in the log. If c7≠0, we get `exp(T*c7)*log(...)` which is not `T*log(...)`. No match.

**Candidate 10:** `T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c1*exp(T*c2) + c3*exp(T*c4) + c5 + c6*log(T*c7 + 1)*log(c8*|epsilon| + 1)`
